< Review>
I checked in right away, but several drivers deep in a line of others checking in at the same time, then waited 7+ hours before finally getting a dock door. After about 8.5 hours, I was finally done. I had a reload in Anaheim that I was supposed to pick up that evening, but the delays here caused my 14 to run out before I had any chance at all of making it to Anaheim that day. I sat another 1.5 after emptying so I would have a fresh 14 to make my way to Anaheim with. I eventually made it to Anaheim only to discover that an after hours dispatcher pulled the load from me and gave it to a driver who was able to pick it up earlier. I didn't have any real issues with employee's attitudes, and the actual unloading time didn't seem to be unreasonably long, hence the reason I decided to actually give them 2 stars. If it had taken longer to unload, I would definitely be giving them only 1 star. This place seriously needs to get more organized with deliveries though. This "free for all" FCFS system they use just doesn't work. Leave FCFS for facilities that don't constantly operate at capacity. I won't willingly come back to this place unless they implement an appointment system to prevent unnecessary staging delays.<//Review>

< text>
So I went in to return a textbook from Chegg. I usually go to the one where my university was located, but I came home and decided to do it here. I should have read the reviews, would of saved me  a horrible experience.
First of all $3 really?? for tape, you apparently have to bring your boxes sealed. From my experiences I have never been charged for tape. Usually the slips are clearly marked to what goes inside, and for some reason mine was not so I did not seal my package. I then asked if they can seal it for me, only to be told that it would be a $3 charge. I then asked why and I was told that it became too "expensive" for the owner to provide "this service". So now they charge you $3 to seal your package or $5 for your own roll.... How in the world does it make sense to charge $3 for a strip of clear tape? A STRIP. A dollar maybe, but come on.
Secondly,  as I went in there were and handful of people waiting before me. I was in no rush, so I didn't mind it at first. Every time a new customer entered they wouldn't look up to greet them, instead they would just look down/ignore them, and just yell out that they will be "eventually be assisted". Then when one clerk decided to see how many people were waiting, she scolded a customer for not realizing that her return was suppose to be at USPS and not UPS. She sarcastically told her she should of read the box more clearly then she wouldn't be wasting her time in line. The customer then asked a question, only to be spoken over and then be ignored.
I seriously don't get the $3 charge, maybe for some you might think  "you should of sealed it prior to returning it". But from all the times I have used UPS (which are several in different locations) they would double check that I was returning the correct product with the correct slip, thus my box would be sealed from them free of charge. I don't think it is fair, especially since I already paid for shipping and handling and now I have to pay and extra $3 for a strip of tape...unbelievable.
Yet overall this team needs help with customer service. No one should be spoken to and treated that way.< /text>

< review>
It's an impressive facility with a full view of the Bay. They have various kinds of gin and vodka to try. I'll be honest that I'm not a fan of gin or vodka so this review is only regarding service and overall experience. I just wanted to see what this place is about and it didn't disappoint. The service is excellent here and they even have tours for you. Everyone seems to be extremely knowledgeable about their products and suggested food pairings or cocktails. One thing is for sure is that their product line is quite smooth compared to most of what I've ever tried outside of the distillery. It's a shame I'm not a fan of gin and vodka, I would probably come here more often. Maybe I'll get a taste for it one day. If I had to choose, i think the green chili vodka would be my top choice. Either way cheers</review>

1581199571816<//date>
<Rating>5<//Rating>< text>
Historic old military base location with a modern distillery repurposing an old building. Nice view across the bay of the San Francisco skyline from the parking lot. Paid tasting of some exceptional spirits inside, and a full selection of their products for purchase.

There were 3 of us and the tasting included 6 tastes each - they had 15 spirits available to taste, so we lined up all 15 to share and then selected 3 more samples to revisit - that worked out great!

Friendly and knowledgeable staff. The absinthe is top notch if you're a fan, which many are. We had a great selection of 4 very different gins that pleased our gin lover. And the new winner of the day was the green chili vodka - what a great nose! Well worth the visit!<//text>

<review>St George Spirits is the home of the local Hanger One vodka and this place is truly in a hanger on an old military base on Alameda 'Island' (complete with some amazing views of the City). We came here for the distillery tour and tasting. Two words to describe the experience "a blast". The whole thing costs $15 per person and you start with a distillery tour in the hanger. Our tour guide was full of fun and energy. Who knew learning about distilling vodka, gin and bourbon could be so much fun! We followed up the tour with the tasting of 6 or 7 of the current spirits which was fun tasting everything and learning about tasting spirits in general (I'm a wine taster but never been spirit tasting before).

Anyone interested in spirit tasting or just looking for a fun way to spend the afternoon should check this place out. We had a huge 20 person birthday group and they were friendly and accommodating. Highly recommended!< /review>< pics>

Gabe Rodriguez<//username>
< review>
For vodka and gin fans, I can't think of a better distillery around. However, for fans of darker liquor, I'd keep looking.

Stationed in the middle of an abandoned industrial district, you'll find St. George's. Though shoddy on the outside, it's modern and chic on the inside. If you're planning a visit, take the tour. For $15 it's not a bad deal and it comes with tastings! The staff were friendly and upbeat, making the tour fun despite the facility not being hugely impressive.

Though I'm not naturally inclined to vodka and gin, the tasting of these spirits were enjoyable. The staff member explained each in great detail, appreciating the finer points and differences. However, beyond those two spirits, there isn't much else. The whisky is average, but the absinthe is awful. It has a licorice taste that I simply wasn't able to consume more than a sip. Not sure who, or on what occasion one would drink this. Expensive bottles, but certainly worth buying a shot glass on the way out.<//review>

<Text>Great way to spend a Saturday afternoon. Tour was both informative and fun, and tastings were a blast. Huge kudos to the St. George team, who has figured out how to make alcohol tours and tastings even more fun than they already are.<//Text></record></dataset><record>
< Review>
First, if you appreciate any type of spirits, reserve a spot on the tour. The tour guides are knowledgeable, but not pedantic. You learn a lot about the distillation process and how flavors are infused. At the end of the tour, you receive a couple of flights of gins, vodkas, and liqueurs, along with a helpful introduction on how to taste spirits. This a great experience with a group. The spirits are reasonably priced, and the staff never steer you to purchase, unlike some crass Napa valley wineries. Lastly, be sure to appreciate the gorgeous views of the San Francisco skyline from the deck outside of of the WWII hangar that is St George. Awesome place!</Review>

<user>108651225409305136803< /user>< name>
Sylvia Lewis</name>
< Date>
1462211993951< /Date>
< Rating>
5<//Rating>
< text>
The tour is awesome and they were extremely accommodating to me and my horrible sense of time. I changed my tour time 3 times over the course of the week, each to a later hour... and still showed up late :(.

However, there's a great brewery with delicious beers and BBQ chicken nachos down the street (while we waited for the 6pm tour) and the tour was definitely worth the wait. Everything they described was spot on and even an alcohol neophyte like myself could taste them (typically, I canNOT taste the "cigarettes" or the "apricot" in wines... but these distilled liquors did a fantastic job of capturing the essential oils of what they're made from).

My favorites:
- Basic vodka: I didn't think I'd like it but it has a wonderful sweet aftertaste that I've never tasted before in a vodka (probably because I'm usually trying to get the shot over with... and because I buy cheap vodka that comes in paper bags)
- Peppery vodka (forgot its name): peppery but doesn't burn your mouth. If you like peppers, this is delicious.
- Terroir gin: Tastes like fermented pine cone and Christmas. I grew up surrounded by pine trees, so somehow this tasted very nostalgic.
- Coffee liquor: My husband thought he'd hate this but it was not super syrupy sweet like other coffee liquors. It tastes more like the famous irish coffee down at Buena Vista cafe in San Francisco.

Unfortunately, we biked so we didn't have a convenient way to bring back the alcohol. We'll be back!< /text>

My husband and I recently went to the Sprouts store @ 4870 Telephone Rd. Ventura, CA 93003 to purchase some salad dressings and Hemp Milk.They're a little pricey, but they have great products that we have not been able to find elsewhere. However, this was a horrible experience.......

When she ran the first card, she looked up and said, "Oh, it ran the whole amount. Well, I pressed $8.50. Have a good night, goodbye." And continued to greet the next customer. My husband then said "Excuse me....you didn't apologize or offer to fix it or anything...I find that quite rude." To which she replied in an exhausted manner, "I can refund it if you want and recharge...". My husband then brought up the point that she didn't even apologize or anything..just sort of brushed it off. We asked to speak with her manager. She replied, "I am the manager." We asked where we could make a complaint. She replied" Excuse me, I am manning the register. I will not be rude to my customer." Then proceeded to ignore us as she greeted the next person in line with a huge smile. I said "But...WE are customers as well..." She continued to ignore us. We then asked a young man close by if there was a manager we could speak to.....he pointed at Konnie. I then walked towards the vitamin section of the store, vocally asking for a manager for help.

Brett"

< Review>
My friends and I came in here for Brunch on a Sunday.  We were immediately impressed by how open the space is.  It's nice to eat and not feel like people are all around you, plenty of space.  The Brunch Menu was pretty interesting, and I'd go back for it again.  The beer menu was kind of amazing, and is probably worth a trip on it's own.

For Food, I got a sandwich modeled after a Montecristo, the whole thing was deep fried.  Everyone at the table tried it and loved it!  Worth it for sure.  I also got a side of their Tater Tots, just plain ones.  But they were well cooked and lightly salted.  Good stuff.

Everyone else seemed to enjoy their food as well.  Definitely heading back and hopefully trying their standard menu, cause it looked amazing.< /Review>

<response>None< /response><gmap_id>0x809053f2cb9715e3:0x938ed884a466dc7e<//gmap_id><Name>Brian Wise< /Name>< text>
I've eaten here 3 times with friends from work. Every time, the food has been delicious and the service is good. Most recently I had the Meatless Wonder veggie burger, which is something they make using fresh ingredients, rather than the mass-produced veggie burger patty you might expect from most places. Tater tots are popular here; but don't expect them to be very special; they taste pretty much like tots do everywhere else on this planet. The omnivores in our group were all pleased with their burgers. Our group also went in for appetizers; the fried cauliflower was top-notch.</text>

<Gmap_id>0x809053f2cb9715e3:0x938ed884a466dc7e</Gmap_id><Review>This place is about the beer, that's it. As I don't care about beer this is about the food and service. My opinion after having lunch there thee times. Two different burgers and a pizza. Let's start with the pizza, not much more than something you would find in the frozen food section of Save Mart. Sour dough thin crust, not very sour by the way, with a light layer of cheese and a sparse topping. Not much to it, not a lot of flavor and over priced and only comes in one size.  Not sure of reasons but if you order pizza plan on 45 to 60 minutes before it gets to your table, to slow for any body with only an hour for lunch. Let's move on to the burgers, there is a few to choose from I've tried two different ones. For a coke and burger plan on spend about $15 plus tip. The burgers only come with tots, yes tots like got as a kid in the school cafeteria. So if you like tots your set, I don't nor do I want to be reminded of tots on a cafeteria tray. Yep it even comes with a tray, if you'd rather have something else than tots for $3 more you can have small plan salad. That's enough about the tater tots, let's talk about the burgers themselves. In a single world average, better burgers to be had elsewhere in downtown Modesto for the same or less money. The service seams to run on the slow side. Don't plan on having your glass refilled, but there is soda dispenser in the back if you get tired of waiting for that refill. Also the place is very very noisy, bad place for a business lunch or to have a conversation at a reasonable voice level. If you are just interested beers this may be the place for you, otherwise better places for lunch in downtown Modesto for the money.<//Review><Date>1501545612325< /Date>< Response>

Came here on a Friday afternoon - the lunch rush was just ending. It was open seating - you could sit in bar area or in the seating tables. We chose the seating tables since most of the bar tables are long in length but short in width. Overall, the customer service was good and knowledgeable about the menu. They helped us by making recommendations on popular dishes and tried to narrow down our taste preferences. Eventually, we went with Cauliflower Bites and going half and half on the pizza. We got half Margerita and half BBQ Chicken on the pizza. I definitely loved the Sriracha Cauliflower Bites as it covered my hot wings craving. The chicken on the BBQ pizza lacked flavor but Margerita pizza was good. It is definitely a good place to eat for some "healthier" alternatives to comfort food. Would come here again!</text>
